[2023-10-03, 14:04:05] Mandinu IIT: can u push if there isnt a remote repository?

No, you cannot push to a remote repository if there is not one. The git push command requires a remote repository to exist in order to push the local commits to.

If you do not have a remote repository, you can create one using the git remote add command. For example, to create a remote repository on GitHub, you would run the following command:

git remote add origin https://github.com/your_username/your_repository_name.git
Once you have created a remote repository, you can push your local commits to it using the git push command.

Here are the steps on how to push your local commits to a remote repository:

Make sure that you have added all of the changes that you want to push to the remote repository. You can do this using the git add command.
Commit your changes to the local repository using the git commit command.
Push your local commits to the remote repository using the git push command.
For example, to push your local commits to the origin remote repository, you would run the following command:

git push origin main
Note: You can also use the git push -u origin main command to push your changes to the remote repository and set it as the upstream repository. This will make it easier to push your future changes to the remote repository.
